\\n859: // selectHost takes a prioritized list of nodes and then picks one\\n860: // in a reservoir sampling manner from the nodes that had the highest score.\\n861: // It also returns the top {count} Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: 0, count)\\n874: \\tsortedNodeScoreList = append(sortedNodeScoreList, heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores))\\n875: \\n876: \\t// This for-loop will continue until all Nodes with the highest retried.\n202: \t\t// This relies on the fact that Error will check if the pod has been bound\n203: \t\t// to a node and if so will not add it back to the unscheduled pods queue\n204: \t\t// (otherwise this would cause an infinite loop).\n205: \t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, framework.AsStatus(err)\n206: \t}\n207: \n208: \t// Run the Reserve method of reserve plugins.\n209: \tif sts := fwk.RunReservePluginsReserve(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost); !sts.IsSuccess() {\n210: \t\t// trigger un-reserve to clean up state associated with the reserved Pod\n211: \t\tfwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n212: \t\tif forgetErr := sched.Cache.ForgetPod(logger, assumedPod); forgetErr != nil {\n213: \t\t\tlogger.Error(forgetErr, \"Scheduler cache ForgetPod failed\")\n214: \t\t}\n215: \n216: \t\tif sts.IsRejected() {\n217: \t\t\tfitErr := &framework.FitError{\n218: \t\t\t\tNumAllNodes: 1,\n219: \t\t\t\tPod:         pod,\n220: \t\t\t\tDiagnosis: framework.Diagnosis{\n221: \t\t\t\t\tNodeToStatusMap: framework.NodeToStatusMap{scheduleResult.SuggestedHost: sts},\n222: \t\t\t\t},\n223: \t\t\t}\n224: \t\t\tfitErr.Diagnosis.AddPluginStatus(sts)\n225: \t\t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, framework.NewStatus(sts.Code()).WithError(fitErr)\n226: \t\t}\n227: \t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, sts\n228: \t}\n229: \n230: \t// Run \"permit\" plugins.\n231: \trunPermitStatus := fwk.RunPermitPlugins(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n232: \tif !runPermitStatus.IsWait() && !runPermitStatus.IsSuccess() {\n233: \t\t// trigger un-reserve to clean up state associated with the reserved Pod\n234: \t\tfwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n235: \t\tif forgetErr := sched.Cache.ForgetPod(logger, assumedPod); forgetErr != nil {\n236: \t\t\tlogger.Error(forgetErr, \"Scheduler cache ForgetPod failed\")\n237: \t\t}\n238: \n239: \t\tif runPermitStatus.IsRejected() {\n240: \t\t\tfitErr := &framework.FitError{\n241: \t\t\t\tNumAllNodes: 1,\n242: \t\t\t\tPod:         pod,\n243: \t\t\t\tDiagnosis: framework.Diagnosis{\n244: \t\t\t\t\tNodeToStatusMap: framework.NodeToStatusMap{scheduleResult.SuggestedHost: runPermitStatus},\n245: \t\t\t\t},\n246: \t\t\t}\n247: \t\t\tfitErr.Diagnosis.AddPluginStatus(runPermitStatus)\n248: \t\t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, framework.NewStatus(runPermitStatus.Code()).WithError(fitErr)\n249: \t\t}\n250: \n251: \t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, runPermitStatus\n252: \t}\n253: \n254: \t// At the end of a successful scheduling cycle, pop and move up Pods if needed.\n255: \tif len(podsToActivate.Map) != 0 {\n256: \t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Activate(logger, podsToActivate.Map)\n257: \t\t// Clear the entries after activation.\n258: \t\tpodsToActivate.Map = make(map[string]*v1.Pod)\n259: \t}\n260: \n261: \treturn scheduleResult, assumedPodInfo, nil\n262: }\n263: \n264: // bindingCycle tries to bind an assumed Pod.\n265: func (sched *Scheduler) bindingCycle(\n266: \tctx context.Context,\n267: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n268: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n269: \tscheduleResult ScheduleResult,\n270: \tassumedPodInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo,\n271: \tstart time.Time,\n272: \tpodsToActivate *framework.PodsToActivate) *framework.Status {\n273: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n274: \n275: \tassumedPod := assumedPodInfo.Pod\n276: \n277: \t// Run \"permit\" plugins.\n278: \tif status := fwk.WaitOnPermit(ctx, assumedPod); !status.IsSuccess() {\n279: \t\tif status.IsRejected() {\n280: \t\t\tfitErr := &framework.FitError{\n281: \t\t\t\tNumAllNodes: 1,\n282: \t\t\t\tPod:         assumedPodInfo.Pod,\n283: \t\t\t\tDiagnosis: framework.Diagnosis{\n284: \t\t\t\t\tNodeToStatusMap:      framework.NodeToStatusMap{scheduleResult.SuggestedHost: status},\n285: \t\t\t\t\tUnschedulablePlugins: sets.New(status.Plugin()),\n286: \t\t\t\t},\n287: \t\t\t}\n288: \t\t\treturn framework.NewStatus(status.Code()).WithError(fitErr)\n289: \t\t}\n290: \t\treturn status\n291: \t}\n292: \n293: \t// Run \"prebind\" plugins.\n294: \tif status := fwk.RunPreBindPlugins(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost); !status.IsSuccess() {\n295: \t\treturn \t}\n302: \n303: \t// Calculating nodeResourceString can be heavy. Avoid it if klog verbosity is below 2.\n304: \tlogger.V(2).Info(\"Successfully bound pod to node\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(assumedPod), \"node\", scheduleResult.SuggestedHost, \"evaluatedNodes\", scheduleResult.EvaluatedNodes, \"feasibleNodes\", scheduleResult.FeasibleNodes)\n305: \tmetrics.PodScheduled(fwk.ProfileName(), metrics.SinceInSeconds(start))\n306: \tmetrics.PodSchedulingAttempts.Observe(float64(assumedPodInfo.Attempts))\n307: \tif assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp != nil {\n308: \t\tmetrics.PodSchedulingDuration.WithLabelValues(getAttemptsLabel(assumedPodInfo)).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(*assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp))\n309: \t\tmetrics.PodSchedulingSLIDuration.WithLabelValues(getAttemptsLabel(assumedPodInfo)).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(*assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp))\n310: \t}\n311: \t// Run \"postbind\" plugins.\n312: \tfwk.RunPostBindPlugins(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n313: \n314: \t// At the end of a successful binding cycle, move up Pods if needed.\n315: \tif len(podsToActivate.Map) != 0 {\n316: \t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Activate(logger, podsToActivate.Map)\n317: \t\t// Unlike the logic in schedulingCycle(), we don't bother deleting the entries\n318: \t\t// as `podsToActivate.Map` is no longer consumed.\n319: \t}\n320: \n321: \treturn nil\n322: }\n323: \n324: func (sched *Scheduler) handleBindingCycleError(\n325: \tctx context.Context,\n326: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n327: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n328: \tpodInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo,\n329: \tstart time.Time,\n330: \tscheduleResult ScheduleResult,\n331: \tstatus *framework.Status) {\n332: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n333: \n334: \tassumedPod := podInfo.Pod\n335: \t// trigger un-reserve plugins to clean up state associated with the reserved Pod\n336: \tfwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n337: \tif forgetErr := sched.Cache.ForgetPod(logger, assumedPod); forgetErr != nil {\n338: \t\tlogger.Error(forgetErr, \"scheduler cache ForgetPod failed\")\n339: \t} else {\n340: \t\t// \"Forget\"ing an assumed Pod in binding cycle should be treated as a PodDelete event,\n341: \t\t// as the assumed Pod had occupied a certain amount of resources in scheduler cache.\n342: \t\t//\n343: \t\t// Avoid moving the assumed Pod itself as it's always Unschedulable.\n344: \t\t// It's intentional to \"defer\" this operation; otherwise MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue() would\n345: \t\t// add this event to in-flight events and thus move the assumed pod to backoffQ anyways if the plugins don't have appropriate QueueingHint.\n346: \t\tif status.IsRejected() {\n347: \t\t\tdefer sched.SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue(logger, internalqueue.AssignedPodDelete, assumedPod, nil, func(pod *v1.Pod) bool {\n348: \t\t\t\treturn assumedPod.UID != pod.UID\n349: \t\t\t})\n350: \t\t} else {\n351: \t\t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue(logger, internalqueue.AssignedPodDelete, assumedPod, nil, nil)\n352: \t\t}\n353: \t}\n354: \n355: \tsched.FailureHandler(ctx, fwk, podInfo, status, clearNominatedNode, start)\n356: }\n357: \n358: func (sched *Scheduler) frameworkForPod(pod *v1.Pod) (framework.Framework, error) {\n359: \tfwk, ok := sched.Profiles[pod.Spec.SchedulerName]\n360: \tif !ok {\n361: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"profile not found for scheduler name %q\", pod.Spec.SchedulerName)\n362: \t}\n363: \treturn fwk, nil\n364: }\n365: \n366: // skipPodSchedule returns true if we could skip scheduling the pod for specified cases.\n367: func (sched *Scheduler) skipPodSchedule(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, pod *v1.Pod) bool {\n368: \t// Case 1: pod is being deleted.\n369: \tif pod.DeletionTimestamp != nil {\n370: \t\tfwk.EventRecorder().Eventf(pod, nil, v1.EventTypeWarning, \"FailedScheduling\", \"Scheduling\", \"skip schedule deleting pod: %v/%v\", pod.Namespace, pod.Name)\n371: \t// An assumed pod can be added again to the scheduling queue if it got an update event\n377: \t// during its previous scheduling cycle but before getting assumed.\n378: \tisAssumed, err := node list.\n388: // If it succeeds, it will return the name of the node.\n389: // If it fails, it will return a FitError with reasons.\n390: func (sched *Scheduler) schedulePod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) (result ScheduleResult, err error) {\n391: \ttrace := utiltrace.New(\"Scheduling\", utiltrace.Field{Key: \"namespace\", Value: pod.Namespace}, utiltrace.Field{Key: \"name\", Value: pod.Name})\n392: \tdefer trace.LogIfLong(100 * time.Millisecond)\n393: \tif err := sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot(klog.FromContext(ctx), sched.nodeInfoSnapshot); err != nil {\n394: \t\treturn result, err\n395: \t}\n396: \ttrace.Step(\"Snapshotting scheduler cache and node infos done\")\n397: \n398: \tif sched.nodeInfoSnapshot.NumNodes() == 0 {\n399: \t\treturn result, ErrNoNodesAvailable\n400: \t}\n401: \n402: \tfeasibleNodes, diagnosis, err := sched.findNodesThatFitPod(ctx, fwk, state, pod)\n403: \tif err != nil {\n404: \t\treturn result, err\n405: \t}\n406: \ttrace.Step(\"Computing predicates done\")\n407: \n408: \tif len(feasibleNodes) == 0 {\n409: \t\treturn result, &framework.FitError{\n410: \t\t\tPod:         pod,\n411: \t\t\tNumAllNodes: sched.nodeInfoSnapshot.NumNodes(),\n412: \t\t\tDiagnosis:   diagnosis,\n413: \t\t}\n414: \t}\n415: \n416: \t// When only one \ttrace.Step(\"Prioritizing done\")\n432: \n433: \treturn ScheduleResult{\n434: \t\tSuggestedHost:  host,\n435: \t\tEvaluatedNodes: len(feasibleNodes) + len(diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap),\n436: \t\tFeasibleNodes:  len(feasibleNodes),\n437: \t}, err\n438: }\n439: \n440: // Filters the nodes to find the ones that fit the pod based on the framework\n441: // filter plugins and filter extenders.\n442: func (sched *Scheduler) findNodesThatFitPod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, framework.Diagnosis, error) {\n443: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n444: \tdiagnosis := framework.Diagnosis{\n445: \t\tNodeToStatusMap: make(framework.NodeToStatusMap),\n446: \t}\n447: \n448: \tallNodes, err := sched.nodeInfoSnapshot.NodeInfos().List()\n449: \tif err != nil {\n450: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n451: \t}\n452: \t// Run \"prefilter\" plugins.\n453: \tpreRes, s := fwk.RunPreFilterPlugins(ctx, state, pod)\n454: \tif !s.IsSuccess() {\n455: \t\tif !s.IsRejected() {\n456: \t\t\treturn nil, diagnosis, s.AsError()\n457: \t\t}\n458: \t\t// All nodes in NodeToStatusMap will have the same status so that they can be handled in the preemption.\n459: \t\t// Some non trivial refactoring is needed to avoid this copy.\n460: \t\tfor _, n := range allNodes {\n461: \t\t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[n.Node().Name] = s\n462: \t\t}\n463: \n464: \t\t// Record the messages from PreFilter in Diagnosis.PreFilterMsg.\n465: \t\tmsg := s.Message()\n466: \t\tdiagnosis.PreFilterMsg = msg\n467: \t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Status after running PreFilter plugins for pod\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"status\", msg)\n468: \t\tdiagnosis.AddPluginStatus(s)\n469: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, nil\n470: \t}\n471: \n472: \t// \"NominatedNodeName\" can potentially be set in a previous scheduling cycle as a result of preemption.\n473: \t// This node is likely the only candidate that will fit the pod, and hence we try it first before iterating over all nodes.\n474: \tif len(pod.Status.NominatedNodeName) > 0 {\n475: \t\tfeasibleNodes, err := sched.evaluateNominatedNode(ctx, pod, fwk, state, diagnosis)\n476: \t\tif err != nil {\n477: \t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Evaluation failed on nominated node\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"node\", pod.Status.NominatedNodeName)\n478: \t\t}\n479: \t\t// Nominated node passes all the filters, scheduler is good to assign this node to the pod.\n480: \t\tif len(feasibleNodes) != 0 {\n481: \t\t\treturn feasibleNodes, diagnosis, nil\n482: \t\t}\n483: \t}\n484: \n485: \tnodes := allNodes\n486: \tif !preRes.AllNodes() {\n487: \t\tnodes = make([]*framework.NodeInfo, 0, len(preRes.NodeNames))\n488: \t\tfor _, n := range allNodes {\n489: \t\t\tif !preRes.NodeNames.Has(n.Node().Name) {\n490: \t\t\t\t// We consider Nodes that are filtered out by PreFilterResult as rejected via UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n491: \t\t\t\t// We have to record them in NodeToStatusMap so that they won't be considered as candidates in the preemption.\n492: \t\t\t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[n.Node().Name] = framework.NewStatus(framework.UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, \"node is filtered out by the prefilter result\")\n493: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n494: \t\t\t}\n495: \t\t\tnodes = append(nodes, n)\n496: \t\t}\n497: \t}\n498: \tfeasibleNodes, err := sched.findNodesThatPassFilters(ctx, fwk, state, pod, &diagnosis, nodes)\n499: \t// always try to update the sched.nextStartNodeIndex regardless of whether an error has occurred\n500: \t// this is helpful to make sure that all the nodes have a chance to be searched\n501: \tprocessedNodes := len(feasibleNodes) + len(diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\n502: \tsched.nextStartNodeIndex = (sched.nextStartNodeIndex + processedNodes) % len(nodes)\n503: \tif err != nil {\n504: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n505: \t}\n506: \n507: \tfeasibleNodesAfterExtender, err := findNodesThatPassExtenders(ctx, sched.Extenders, pod, feasibleNodes, diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\n508: \tif err != nil {\n509: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n510: \t}\n511: \tif len(feasibleNodesAfterExtender) != len(feasibleNodes) {\n512: \t\t// Extenders filtered out some nodes.\n513: \t\t//\n514: \t\t// Extender doesn't support any kind of requeueing feature like EnqueueExtensions in the scheduling framework.\n515: \t\t// When Extenders reject some Nodes and the pod ends up being unschedulable,\n516: \t\t// we put framework.ExtenderName to pInfo.UnschedulablePlugins.\n517: \t\t// This Pod will be requeued from unschedulable pod pool to activeQ/backoffQ\n518: \t\t// by any kind of cluster events.\n519: \t\t// https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/122019\n520: \t\tif diagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins == nil {\n521: \t\t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins = sets.New[string]()\n522: \t\t}\n523: \t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins.Insert(framework.ExtenderName)\n524: \t}\n525: \n526: \treturn feasibleNodesAfterExtender, diagnosis, nil\n527: }\n528: \n529: func (sched *Scheduler) evaluateNominatedNode(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, diagnosis framework.Diagnosis) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n530: \tnnn := nil\n547: }\n548: \n549: // hasScoring checks if scoring nodes is configured.\n550: func (sched *Scheduler) hasScoring(fwk framework.Framework) bool {\n551: \tif fwk.HasScorePlugins() {\n552: \n562: // hasExtenderFilters checks if any extenders filter nodes.\n563: func (sched *Scheduler) hasExtenderFilters() bool {\n564: \tfor _, extender := range sched.Extenders {\n565: \t\tif *Scheduler) findNodesThatPassFilters(\n574: \tctx context.Context,\n575: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n576: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n577: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n578: \tdiagnosis *framework.Diagnosis,\n579: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n580: \tnumAllNodes := len(nodes)\n581: \tnumNodesToFind := sched.numFeasibleNodesToFind(fwk.PercentageOfNodesToScore(), int32(numAllNodes))\n582: \tif !sched.hasExtenderFilters() && !sched.hasScoring(fwk) {\n583: \t\tnumNodesToFind = 1\n584: \t}\n585: \n586: \t// Create feasible list with enough space to avoid growing it\n587: \t// and allow assigning.\n588: \tfeasibleNodes := make([]*framework.NodeInfo, numNodesToFind)\n589: \n590: \tif \t}\n596: \n597: \terrCh := parallelize.NewErrorChannel()\n598: \tvar feasibleNodesLen int32\n599: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n600: \tdefer cancel()\n601: \n602: \ttype nodeStatus struct {\n603: \t\tnode   string\n604: \t\tstatus *framework.Status\n605: \t}\n606: \tresult := make([]*nodeStatus, numAllNodes)\n607: \tcheckNode := func(i int) {\n608: \t\t// We check the nodes starting from where we left off in the previous scheduling cycle,\n609: \t\t// this is to make sure all nodes have the same chance of being examined across pods.\n610: \t\tnodeInfo := nodes[(sched.nextStartNodeIndex+i)%numAllNodes]\n611: \t\tstatus := fwk.RunFilterPluginsWithNominatedPods(ctx, state, pod, nodeInfo)\n612: \t\tif status.Code() == framework.Error {\n613: \t\t\terrCh.SendErrorWithCancel(status.AsError(), cancel)\n614: \t\t\treturn\n615: \t\t}\n616: \t\tif status.IsSuccess() {\n617: \t\t\tlength := atomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, 1)\n618: \t\t\tif length > numNodesToFind {\n619: \t\t\t\tcancel()\n620: \t\t\t\tatomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, -1)\n621: \t\t\t} else {\n622: \t\t\t\tfeasibleNodes[length-1] = nodeInfo\n623: \t\t\t}\n624: \t\t} else {\n625: \t\t\tresult[i] = &nodeStatus{node: nodeInfo.Node().Name, status: status}\n626: \t\t}\n627: \t}\n628: \n629: \tbeginCheckNode := time.Now()\n630: \tstatusCode := framework.Success\n631: \tdefer func() {\n632: \t\t// We record Filter extension point latency here instead of in framework.go because framework.RunFilterPlugins\n633: \t\t// function is called for each node, whereas we want to have an overall latency for all nodes per scheduling cycle.\n634: \t\t// Note that this latency also includes latency for `addNominatedPods`, which calls framework.RunPreFilterAddPod.\n635: \t\tmetrics.FrameworkExtensionPointDuration.WithLabelValues(metrics.Filter, statusCode.String(), fwk.ProfileName()).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(beginCheckNode))\n636: \t}()\n637: \n638: \t// Stops searching for more nodes once the configured number of feasible nodes\n639: \t// are found.\n640: \tfwk.Parallelizer().Until(ctx, numAllNodes, checkNode, metrics.Filter)\n641: \tfeasibleNodes = feasibleNodes[:feasibleNodesLen]\n642: \tfor _, item := range result {\n643: \t\tif item == nil {\n644: \t\t\tcontinue\n645: \t\t}\n646: \t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[item.node] = item.status\n647: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n654: }\n655: \n656: // numFeasibleNodesToFind returns the number of feasible nodes that once found, the scheduler stops\n657: // its search for more feasible nodes.\n658: func (sched *Scheduler) numFeasibleNodesToFind(percentageOfNodesToScore *int32, numAllNodes int32) (numNodes int32) {\n659: \tif numAllNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n660: \t\treturn numAllNodes\n661: \t}\n662: \n663: \t// Use profile percentageOfNodesToScore if it's set. Otherwise, use global percentageOfNodesToScore.\n664: \tvar percentage int32\n665: \tif percentageOfNodesToScore != nil {\n666: \t\tpercentage = *percentageOfNodesToScore\n667: \t} else {\n668: \t\tpercentage = sched.percentageOfNodesToScore\n669: \t}\n670: \n671: \tif percentage == 0 {\n672: \t\tpercentage = int32(50) - numAllNodes/125\n673: \t\tif percentage < minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind {\n674: \t\t\tpercentage = minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind\n675: \t\t}\n676: \t}\n677: \n678: \tnumNodes = numAllNodes * percentage / 100\n679: \tif numNodes < Success means that plugin ran correctly and found pod schedulable.\\n79: \\t// NOTE: A nil status is also considered as \\\"Success\\\".\\n80: \\tSuccess Code = iota\\n81: \\t// Error is one of the and\\n97: \\t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\\n98: \\t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\\n105: \\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\\n106: \\tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\n107: \\t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\\n108: \\tWait\\n109: \\t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\\n110: \\t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\\n111: \\t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\\n112: \\t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\\n113: \\tSkip\\n114: \\t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\\n115: \\t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\\n116: \\t//\\n117: \\t// For example, the DRA plugin sometimes needs to wait for the external device driver\\n118: \\t// to provision the resource for the Pod.\\n119: \\t// It's different from when to bool\\n347: \\n348: // QueueSortPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"QueueSort\\\" plugins.\\n349: // These plugins are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue. Only one queue sort\\n350: // plugin may be enabled at a time.\\n351: type QueueSortPlugin interface {\\n352: \\tPlugin\\n353: \\t// Less are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue.\\n354: \\tLess(*QueuedPodInfo, *QueuedPodInfo) bool\\n355: }\\n356: \\n357: // EnqueueExtensions is an optional interface that plugins can implement to efficiently\\n358: // move unschedulable Pods in internal scheduling queues.\\n359: // In the scheduler, Pods can be unschedulable by PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins,\\n360: // and Pods rejected by these plugins are requeued based on this extension point.\\n361: // Failures from other extension points are regarded as temporal errors (e.g., network failure),\\n362: // and the scheduler requeue Pods without this extension point - always requeue Pods to activeQ after backoff.\\n363: // This is because such temporal errors cannot be resolved by specific cluster events,\\n364: // and we have no choise but keep retrying scheduling until the failure is resolved.\\n365: //\\n366: // Plugins that make pod unschedulable (PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins) should implement this interface,\\n367: // otherwise the default implementation will be used, which is less efficient in requeueing Pods rejected by the plugin.\\n368: // And, if plugins other than above extension points support this interface, they are just ignored.\\n369: type EnqueueExtensions interface {\\n370: \\tPlugin\\n371: \\t// EventsToRegister returns a series of possible events that may cause a Pod\\n372: \\t// failed by this plugin schedulable. Each event has a callback function that\\n373: \\t// filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\\n374: \\t// The events will be registered when instantiating the internal scheduling queue,\\n375: \\t// and leveraged to build event handlers dynamically.\\n376: \\t// Note: the returned list needs to be static (not depend on configuration parameters);\\n377: \\t// otherwise it would lead to undefined behavior.\\n378: \\t//\\n379: \\t// Appropriate implementation of this function will make Pod's re-scheduling accurate and performant.\\n380: \\tEventsToRegister() []ClusterEventWithHint\\n381: }\\n382: \\n383: // PreFilterExtensions is an interface that is included in plugins that allow specifying\\n384: // callbacks to make incremental updates to its supposedly pre-calculated\\n385: // state.\\n386: type PreFilterExtensions interface {\\n387: \\t// AddPod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\\n388: \\t// of adding podToAdd to the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\\n389: \\tAddPod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToAdd *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\\n390: \\t// RemovePod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\\n391: \\t// of removing podToRemove from the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\\n392: \\tRemovePod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToRemove *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\\n393: }\\n394: \\n395: // PreFilterPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"PreFilter\\\" plugins.\\n396: // These plugins are called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle.\\n397: type PreFilterPlugin interface {\\n398: \\tPlugin\\n399: \\t// PreFilter is called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. All PreFilter\\n400: \\t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. PreFilter could optionally\\n401: declares a list of nodes and their scores.\\n44: type NodeScoreList []NodeScore\\n45: \\n46: // NodeScore is a struct with node name and score.\\n47: type NodeScore struct {\\n48: \\tName  string\\n49: \\tScore int64\\n50: }\\n51: \\n52: // NodeToStatusMap declares map from node name to its status.\\n53: type NodeToStatusMap map[string]*Status\\n54: \\n55: // NodePluginScores is a struct with node name and scores for that node.\\n56: type NodePluginScores struct {\\n57: \\t// Name is node name.\\n58: \\tName string\\n59: \\t// Scores is scores from plugins and extenders.\\n60: \\tScores []PluginScore\\n61: \\t// TotalScore is the total score in Scores.\\n62: \\tTotalScore int64\\n63: }\\n64: \\n65: // PluginScore is a struct with plugin/extender name and score.\\n66: type PluginScore struct {\\n67: \\t// Name is the name of plugin or extender.\\n68: \\tName  string\\n69: \\tScore int64\\n70: }\\n71: \\n72: // Code is the Status code/type which is returned from plugins.\\n73: type Code int\\n74: \\n75: // These are predefined codes used in a Status.\\n76: // Note: when you add a new status, you have to add it in `codes` slice below.\\n77: const (\\n78: \\t// Success means that plugin ran correctly and found pod schedulable.\\n79: \\t// NOTE: A nil status is also considered as \\\"Success\\\".\\n80: \\tSuccess Code = iota\\n81: \\t// Error is one of the failures, used for internal plugin errors, unexpected input, etc.\\n82: \\t// Plugin shouldn't return this code for expected failures, like Unschedulable.\\n83: \\t// Since it's the unexpected failure, the scheduling queue registers the pod without unschedulable plugins.\\n84: \\t// Meaning, the Pod will be requeued to activeQ/backoffQ soon.\\n85: \\tError\\n86: \\t// Unschedulable is one of the failures, used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable.\\n87: \\t// If it's returned from PreFilter or Filter, the scheduler might attempt to\\n88: \\t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\\n89: \\t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\\n90: \\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\\n91: \\t//\\n92: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n93: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\\n94: \\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\\n95: \\tUnschedulable\\n96: \\t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable and\\n97: \\t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\\n98: \\t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this status.\\n99: \\t// Plugins should return Unschedulable if it is possible that the pod can get scheduled\\n100: \\t// after running other postFilter plugins.\\n101: \\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\\n102: \\t//\\n103: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n104: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\\n105: \\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\\n106: \\tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\n107: \\t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\\n108: \\tWait\\n109: \\t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\\n110: \\t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\\n111: \\t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\\n112: \\t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\\n113: \\tSkip\\n114: \\t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\\n115: \\t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\\n116: \\t//\\n117: \\t// For example, the DRA plugin sometimes needs to wait for the external device driver\\n118: \\t// to provision the resource for the Pod.\\n119: \\t// It's different from when to return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable,\\n120: \\t// because in this case, the scheduler decides where the Pod can go successfully,\\n121: \\t// but we need to wait for the external component to do something based on that scheduling result.\\n122: \\t//\\n123: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n124: \\t// In the case of returning Pending, we cannot say the scheduling cycle is wasted\\n125: \\t// because the scheduling result is used to proceed the Pod's scheduling forward,\\n126: \\t// that particular scheduling cycle is failed though.\\n127: \\t// So, Pods rejected by such reasons don't need to suffer a penalty (backoff).\\n128: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Pending in the last scheduling,\\n129: \\t// the Pod goes to activeQ directly ignoring backoff.\\n130: \\tPending\\n131: )\\n132: \\n133: // This list should be exactly the same as the codes iota defined above in the same order.\\n134: var codes = []string{\\\"Success\\\", \\\"Error\\\", \\\"Unschedulable\\\", \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\", \\\"Wait\\\", \\\"Skip\\\", \\\"Pending\\\"}\\n135: \\n136: func (c Code) String() string {\\n137: \\treturn codes[c]\\n138: }\\n139: \\n140: const (\\n141: \\t// MaxNodeScore is the maximum score a Score plugin is expected to return.\\n142: \\tMaxNodeScore int64 = 100\\n143: \\n144: \\t// MinNodeScore is the minimum score a Score plugin is expected to return.\\n145: \\tMinNodeScore int64 = 0\\n146: \\n147: \\t// MaxTotalScore is the maximum total score.\\n148: \\tMaxTotalScore int64 = math.MaxInt64\\n149: )\\n150: \\n151: // PodsToActivateKey is a reserved state key for stashing pods.\\n152: // If the stashed pods are present in unschedulablePods or backoffQ，they will be\\n153: // activated (i.e., moved to activeQ) in two phases:\\n154: // - end of a scheduling cycle if it succeeds (will be cleared from `PodsToActivate` if activated)\\n155: // - end of a binding cycle if it succeeds\\n156: var PodsToActivateKey StateKey = \\\"kubernetes.io/pods-to-activate\\\"\\n157: \\n158: // PodsToActivate stores pods to be activated.\\n159: type PodsToActivate struct {\\n160: \\tsync.Mutex\\n161: \\t// Map is keyed with namespaced pod name, and valued with the pod.\\n162: \\tMap map[string]*v1.Pod\\n163: }\\n164: \\n165: // Clone just returns the same state.\\n166: func (s *PodsToActivate) Clone() StateData {\\n167: \\treturn s\\n168: }\\n169: \\n170: // NewPodsToActivate instantiates a PodsToActivate object.\\n171: func NewPodsToActivate() *PodsToActivate {\\n172: \\treturn &PodsToActivate{Map: make(map[string]*v1.Pod)}\\n173: }\\n174: \\n175: // Status indicates the result of running a plugin. code is Success, all the other fields should be empty.\\n179: // NOTE: A nil Status is also considered as Success.\\n180: type Status struct {\\n181: \\tcode    Code\\n182: \\treasons []string\\n183: \\terr     error\\n184: \\t// plugin is an optional field that records the plugin name causes this status.\\n185: \\t// It's set by the framework when code is Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable or Pending.\\n186: \\tplugin string\\n187: }\\n188: \\n189: func (s *Status) WithError(err error) *Status {\\n190: \\ts.err = err\\n191: \\treturn s\\n192: }\\n193: \\n194: // Code returns code of the Status.\\n195: func (s *Status) Code() Code {\\n196: \\tif s == nil {\\n197: \\t\\treturn Success\\n198: \\t}\\n199: \\treturn s.code\\n200: }\\n201: \\n202: // Message returns a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\\n203: func (s *Status) Message() string {\\n204: \\tif s == nil {\\n205: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\"\\n206: \\t}\\n207: \\treturn strings.Join(s.Reasons(), \\\", \\\")\\n208: }\\n209: \\n210: // SetPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin.\\n211: func (s *Status) SetPlugin(plugin string) {\\n212: \\ts.plugin = plugin\\n213: }\\n214: \\n215: // WithPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin,\\n216: // and returns the given status object.\\n217: func (s *Status) WithPlugin(plugin string) *Status {\\n218: \\ts.SetPlugin(plugin)\\n219: \\treturn s\\n220: }\\n221: \\n222: // Plugin returns the plugin name which caused this status.\\n223: func (s *Status) Plugin() string {\\n224: \\treturn s.plugin\\n225: }\\n226: \\n227: // Reasons returns reasons of the Status.\\n228: func (s *Status) Reasons() []string {\\n229: \\tif s.err != nil {\\n230: \\t\\treturn append([]string{s.err.Error()}, s.reasons...)\\n231: \\t}\\n232: \\treturn s.reasons\\n233: }\\n234: \\n235: // AppendReason appends given reason to the Status.\\n236: func (s *Status) AppendReason(reason string) {\\n237: \\ts.reasons = append(s.reasons, reason)\\n238: }\\n239: \\n240: // IsSuccess returns true if and only if \\\"Status\\\" is nil or Code is \\\"Success\\\".\\n241: func (s *Status) IsSuccess() bool \\treturn s.Code() == Skip\\n253: }\\n254: \\n255: // IsRejected returns true if \\\"Status\\\" is Unschedulable (Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, or Pending).\\n256: func (s *Status) }\\n272: \\n273: // Equal checks equality of two statuses. This is useful for testing with\\n274: // cmp.Equal.\\n275: func (s *Status) Equal(x *Status) bool {\\n276: \\tif s == nil || x == nil {\\n277: \\t\\treturn s.IsSuccess() && x.IsSuccess()\\n278: is one of the failures, used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable.\n87: \t// If it's returned from PreFilter or Filter, the scheduler might attempt to\n88: \t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\n89: \t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\n90: \t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n91: \t//\n92: \t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n93: \t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\n94: \t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n95: \tUnschedulable\n96: \t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable and\n97: \t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\n98: \t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this status.\n99: \t// Plugins should return Unschedulable if it is possible that the pod can get scheduled\n100: \t// after running other postFilter plugins.\n101: \t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n102: \t//\n103: \t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n104: \t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\n105: \t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n106: \tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n107: \t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\n108: \tWait\n109: \t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\n110: \t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\n111: \t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\n112: \t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\n113: \tSkip\n114: \t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\n115: \t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\n116: \t//\n117: \t// For example, the DRA plugin sometimes needs to wait for the external device driver\n118: \t// to provision the resource for the Pod.\n119: \t// It's different from when to return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable,\n120: \t// because in this case, the scheduler decides where the Pod can go successfully,\n121: \t// but we need to wait for the external component to do something based on that scheduling result.\n122: \t//\n123: \t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n124: \t// In the case of returning Pending, we cannot say the scheduling cycle is wasted\n125: \t// because the scheduling result is used to proceed the Pod's scheduling forward,\n126: \t// that particular scheduling cycle is failed though.\n127: \t// So, Pods rejected by such reasons don't need to suffer a penalty (backoff).\n128: scheduling cycle:\n673: \t// - There is no guarantee that the information remains unchanged in the binding phase of scheduling.\n674: \t//   So, plugins shouldn't use it in the binding cycle If the key is not\n101: // present, ErrNotFound is returned.\n102: //\n103: // See CycleState for notes on concurrency.\n104: func (c *CycleState) Read(key StateKey) (StateData, error) {\n105: \tif v, ok := c.storage.Load(key); ok {\n106: \t\treturn v.(StateData), nil\n107: \t}\n108: \treturn nil, ErrNotFound\n109: }\n110: \n111: // Write stores the given \"val\" in CycleState with the given \"key\".\n112: //\n113: // See CycleState for notes on concurrency.\n114: func (c *CycleState) Write(key StateKey, val StateData) {\n115: \tc.storage.Store(key, val)\n116: }\n117: \n118: // Delete deletes data with the given key from CycleState.\n119: //\n120: // See CycleState for notes on concurrency.\n121: func (c *CycleState) Delete(key StateKey) {\n122: \tc.storage.Delete(key)\n123: }\n124: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.30.0@917ed05e89979783903c4ca4563f0fc4120df4e2/-/blob/pkg/scheduler/framework/cycle_state.go"}}}

If a pod stays in unschedulablePods\\n59: \\t// for longer than this value, the pod will be moved from unschedulablePods to\\n60: \\t// backoffQ or activeQ. If this value is empty, the default value (5min)\\n61: \\t// will be used.\\n62: \\tDefaultPodMaxInUnschedulablePodsDuration time.Duration = 5 * time.Minute\\n63: \\t// Scheduling queue names\\n64: \\tactiveQ           = \\\"Active\\\"\\n65: \\tbackoffQ          = \\\"Backoff\\\"\\n66: \\tunschedulablePods = \\\"Unschedulable\\\"\\n67: \\n68: \\tpreEnqueue = \\\"PreEnqueue\\\"\\n69: )\\n70: \\n71: const (\\n72: \\t// DefaultPodInitialBackoffDuration is the default value for the initial backoff duration\\n73: \\t// for unschedulable pods. To change the default podInitialBackoffDurationSeconds used by the\\n74: \\t// scheduler, update the ComponentConfig value in defaults.go\\n75: \\tDefaultPodInitialBackoffDuration time.Duration = 1 * time.Second\\n76: \\t// DefaultPodMaxBackoffDuration is the default value for the max backoff duration\\n77: \\t// for unschedulable pods. To change the default podMaxBackoffDurationSeconds used by the\\n78: \\t// scheduler, update the ComponentConfig value in defaults.go\\n79: \\tDefaultPodMaxBackoffDuration time.Duration = 10 * time.Second\\n80: )\\n81: \\n82: // PreEnqueueCheck is a function type. It's used to build functions that\\n83: // run against a Pod and the caller can choose to enqueue or skip the Pod\\n84: // by the checking result.\\n85: type PreEnqueueCheck func(pod *v1.Pod) bool\\n86: \\n87: // SchedulingQueue is an interface for a queue to store pods waiting to be scheduled.\\n88: // The interface follows a pattern similar to cache.FIFO and cache.Heap and\\n89: // makes it easy to use those data structures as a SchedulingQueue.\\n90: type SchedulingQueue interface {\\n91: \\tframework.PodNominator\\n92: \\tAdd(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod) error\\n93: \\t// Activate moves the given pods to activeQ iff they're in unschedulablePods or backoffQ.\\n94: \\t// The passed-in pods are originally compiled from plugins that want to activate Pods,\\n95: \\t// by injecting the pods through a reserved CycleState struct (PodsToActivate).\\n96: \\tActivate(logger klog.Logger, pods map[string]*v1.Pod)\\n97: \\t// AddUnschedulableIfNotPresent adds an unschedulable pod back to scheduling queue.\\n98: \\t// The podSchedulingCycle represents the current scheduling cycle number which can be\\n99: \\t// returned by calling SchedulingCycle().\\n100: \\tAddUnschedulableIfNotPresent(logger klog.Logger, pod *framework.QueuedPodInfo, podSchedulingCycle int64) error\\n101: \\t// SchedulingCycle returns the current number of scheduling cycle which is\\n102: \\t// cached by scheduling queue. Normally, incrementing this number whenever\\n103: \\t// a pod is popped (e.g. called Pop()) is enough.\\n104: \\tSchedulingCycle() int64\\n105: \\t// Pop removes the head of the queue and returns it. It blocks if the\\n106: \\t// queue is empty and waits until a new item is added to the queue.\\n107: \\tPop(logger klog.Logger) (*framework.QueuedPodInfo, error)\\n108: \\t// Done must be called for pod returned by Pop. This allows the queue to\\n109: \\t// keep track of which pods are currently being processed.\\n110: \\tDone(types.UID)\\n111: \\tUpdate(logger klog.Logger, oldPod, newPod *v1.Pod) error\\n112: \\tDelete(pod *v1.Pod) error\\n113: \\t// TODO(sanposhiho): move all PreEnqueueCkeck to Requeue and delete it from this parameter eventually.\\n114: \\t// Some PreEnqueueCheck include event filtering logic based on some in-tree plugins\\n115: \\t// and it affect badly to other plugins.\\n116: \\t// See https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/110175\\n117: \\tMoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue(logger klog.Logger, event framework.ClusterEvent, oldObj, newObj interface{}, preCheck PreEnqueueCheck)\\n118: \\tAssignedPodAdded(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod)\\n119: \\tAssignedPodUpdated(logger klog.Logger, oldPod, newPod *v1.Pod)\\n120: \\tPendingPods() ([]*v1.Pod, string)\\n121: \\tPodsInActiveQ() []*v1.Pod\\n122: \\t// Close closes the SchedulingQueue so that the goroutine which is\\n123: \\t// waiting to pop items can exit gracefully.\\n124: \\tClose()\\n125: \\t// Run starts the goroutines managing the queue.\\n126: \\tRun(logger klog.Logger)\\n127: }\\n128: \\n129: // NewSchedulingQueue initializes a priority queue as a new scheduling queue.\\n130: func NewSchedulingQueue(\\n131: \\tlessFn framework.LessFunc,\\n132: \\tinformerFactory informers.SharedInformerFactory,\\n133: \\topts ...Option) SchedulingQueue {\\n134: \\treturn NewPriorityQueue(lessFn, informerFactory, opts...)\\n135: }\\n136: \\n137: // NominatedNodeName returns nominated node name of a Pod.\\n138: func NominatedNodeName(pod *v1.Pod) string {\\n139: \\treturn pod.Status.NominatedNodeName\\n140: }\\n141: \\n142: // PriorityQueue implements a scheduling queue.\\n143: // The head of PriorityQueue is the highest priority pending pod. This structure\\n144: // has two sub queues and a additional data structure, namely: activeQ,\\n145: // backoffQ and unschedulablePods.\\n146: //   - activeQ holds pods that are being considered for scheduling.\\n147: //   - backoffQ holds pods that moved from unschedulablePods and will move to\\n148: //     activeQ when their backoff periods complete.\\n149: //   - unschedulablePods holds pods that were already attempted for scheduling and\\n150: //     are currently determined to be unschedulable.\\n151: type PriorityQueue struct {\\n152: \\t*nominator\\n153: \\n154: \\tstop  chan struct{}\\n155: \\tclock clock.Clock\\n156: \\n157: \\t// pod initial backoff duration.\\n158: \\tpodInitialBackoffDuration time.Duration\\n159: \\t// pod maximum backoff duration.\\n160: \\tpodMaxBackoffDuration time.Duration\\n161: \\t// the maximum time a pod can stay in the unschedulablePods.\\n162: \\tpodMaxInUnschedulablePodsDuration time.Duration\\n163: \\n164: \\tcond sync.Cond\\n165: \\n166: \\t// inFlightPods holds the UID of all pods which have been popped out for which Done\\n167: \\t// hasn't been called yet - in other words, all pods that are currently being\\n168: \\t// processed (being scheduled, in permit, or in the binding cycle).\\n169: \\t//\\n170: \\t// The values in the map are the entry of each pod in the inFlightEvents list.\\n171: \\t// The value of that entry is the *v1.Pod at the time that scheduling of that\\n172: \\t// pod started, which can be useful for logging or debugging.\\n173: \\tinFlightPods map[types.UID]*list.Element\\n174: \\n175: \\t// inFlightEvents holds the events received by the scheduling queue\\n176: \\t// (entry value is clusterEvent) together with in-flight pods (entry\\n177: \\t// value is *v1.Pod). Entries get added at the end while the mutex is\\n178: \\t// locked, so they get serialized.\\n179: \\t//\\n180: \\t// The pod entries are added in Pop and used to track which events\\n181: \\t// occurred after the pod scheduling attempt for that pod started.\\n182: \\t// They get removed when the scheduling attempt is done, at which\\n183: \\t// point all events that occurred in the meantime are processed.\\n184: \\t//\\n185: \\t// After removal of a pod, events at the start of the list are no\\n186: \\t// longer needed because all of the other in-flight pods started\\n187: \\t// later. Those events can be removed.\\n188: \\tinFlightEvents *list.List\\n189: \\n190: \\t// activeQ is heap structure that scheduler actively looks at to find pods to\\n191: \\t// schedule. Head of heap is the highest priority pod.\\n192: \\tactiveQ *heap.Heap\\n193: \\t// podBackoffQ is a heap ordered by backoff expiry. Pods which have completed backoff\\n194: \\t// are popped from this heap before the scheduler looks at activeQ\\n195: \\tpodBackoffQ *heap.Heap\\n196: \\t// unschedulablePods holds pods that have been tried and determined unschedulable.\\n197: \\tunschedulablePods *UnschedulablePods\\n198: \\t// schedulingCycle represents sequence number of scheduling cycle and is incremented\\n199: \\t// when a pod is popped.\\n200: \\tschedulingCycle int64\\n201: \\t// moveRequestCycle caches the sequence number of scheduling cycle when we\\n202: \\t// received a move request. Unschedulable pods in and before this scheduling\\n203: \\t// cycle will be put back to activeQueue if we were trying to schedule them\\n204: \\t// when we received move request.\\n205: \\t// TODO: this will be removed after SchedulingQueueHint goes to stable and the feature gate is removed.\\n206: \\tmoveRequestCycle int64\\n207: \\n208: \\t// preEnqueuePluginMap is keyed with profile name, valued with registered preEnqueue plugins.\\n209: \\tpreEnqueuePluginMap map[string][]framework.PreEnqueuePlugin\\n210: \\t// queueingHintMap is keyed with profile name, valued with registered queueing hint functions.\\n211: \\tqueueingHintMap QueueingHintMapPerProfile\\n212: \\n213: \\t// closed indicates that the queue is closed.\\n214: \\t// It is mainly used to let Pop() exit its control loop while waiting for an item.\\n215: \\tclosed bool\\n216: \\n217: \\tnsLister listersv1.NamespaceLister\\n218: \\n219: \\tmetricsRecorder metrics.MetricAsyncRecorder\\n220: \\t// pluginMetricsSamplePercent is the percentage of plugin metrics to be sampled.\\n221: \\tpluginMetricsSamplePercent int\\n222: \\n223: \\t// isSchedulingQueueHintEnabled indicates whether the feature gate for the scheduling queue is enabled.\\n224: \\tisSchedulingQueueHintEnabled bool\\n225: }\\n226: \\n227: // QueueingHintFunction is the wrapper of QueueingHintFn that has PluginName.\\n228: type This structure\n144: // has two sub queues and a additional data structure, namely: activeQ,\n145: // backoffQ and unschedulablePods.\n146: //   - activeQ holds pods that are being considered for scheduling.\n147: //   - backoffQ holds pods that moved from unschedulablePods and will move to\n148: //     activeQ when their backoff periods complete.\n149: //   - unschedulablePods holds pods that were already attempted for scheduling and\n150: //     are currently determined to be unschedulable.\n151: type PriorityQueue struct {\n152: \t*nominator\n153: \n154: \tstop  chan struct{}\n155: \tclock clock.Clock\n156: \n157: \t// pod initial backoff duration.\n158: \tpodInitialBackoffDuration time.Duration\n159: \t// pod maximum backoff duration.\n160: \tpodMaxBackoffDuration time.Duration\n161: \t// the maximum time a pod can stay in the unschedulablePods.\n162: \tpodMaxInUnschedulablePodsDuration time.Duration\n163: \n164: \tcond sync.Cond\n165: \n166: \t// inFlightPods holds the UID of all pods which have been popped out for which Done\n167: \t// hasn't been called yet - in other words, all pods that are currently being\n168: \t// processed (being scheduled, in permit, or in the binding cycle).\n169: \t//\n170: \t// The values in the map are the entry of each pod in the inFlightEvents list.\n171: \t// The value of that entry is the *v1.Pod at the time that scheduling of that\n172: \t// pod started, which can be useful for logging or debugging.\n173: \tinFlightPods map[types.UID]*list.Element\n174: \n175: \t// inFlightEvents holds the events received by the scheduling queue\n176: \t// (entry value is clusterEvent) together with in-flight pods (entry\n177: \t// value is *v1.Pod). Entries get added at the end while the mutex is\n178: \t// locked, so they get serialized.\n179: \t//\n180: \t// The pod entries are added in Pop and used to track which events\n181: \t// occurred after the pod scheduling attempt for that pod started.\n182: \t// They get removed when the scheduling attempt is done, at which\n183: \t// point all events that occurred in the meantime are processed.\n184: \t//\n185: \t// After removal of a pod, events at the start of the list are no\n186: \t// longer needed because all of the other in-flight pods started\n187: \t// later. Those events can be removed.\n188: \tinFlightEvents *list.List\n189: \n190: \t// activeQ is heap structure that scheduler actively looks at to find pods to\n191: \t// schedule. Head of heap is the highest priority pod.\n192: \tactiveQ *heap.Heap\n193: \t// podBackoffQ is a heap ordered by backoff expiry. Pods which have completed backoff\n194: \t// are popped from this heap before the scheduler looks at activeQ\n195: \tpodBackoffQ *heap.Heap\n196: \t// unschedulablePods holds pods that have been tried and determined unschedulable.\n197: \tunschedulablePods *UnschedulablePods\n198: \t// schedulingCycle represents sequence number of scheduling cycle and is incremented\n199: \t// when a pod is popped.\n200: \tschedulingCycle int64\n201: \t// moveRequestCycle caches the sequence number of scheduling cycle when we\n202: \t// received a move request. Unschedulable pods in and before this scheduling\n203: \t// cycle will be put back to activeQueue if we were trying to schedule them\n204: \t// when we received move request.\n205: \t// TODO: this will be removed after SchedulingQueueHint goes to stable and the feature gate is removed.\n206: \tmoveRequestCycle int64\n207: \n208: \t// preEnqueuePluginMap is keyed with profile name, valued with registered preEnqueue plugins.\n209: \tpreEnqueuePluginMap map[string][]framework.PreEnqueuePlugin\n210: \t// queueingHintMap is keyed with profile name, valued with registered queueing hint functions.\n211: \tqueueingHintMap QueueingHintMapPerProfile\n212: \n213: \t// closed indicates that the queue is closed.\n214: \t// It is mainly used to let Pop() exit its control loop while waiting for an item.\n215: \tclosed bool\n216: \n217: \tnsLister listersv1.NamespaceLister\n218: \n219: \tmetricsRecorder metrics.MetricAsyncRecorder\n220: \t// pluginMetricsSamplePercent is the percentage of plugin metrics to be sampled.\n221: \tpluginMetricsSamplePercent int\n222: \n223: \t// isSchedulingQueueHintEnabled indicates whether the feature gate for the scheduling queue is enabled.\n224: \tisSchedulingQueueHintEnabled bool\n225: }\n226: \n227: // QueueingHintFunction is the wrapper of QueueingHintFn that has PluginName.\n228: type QueueingHintFunction struct {\n229: \tPluginName {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_019wksBNxvW42jpo7AfP4mF8","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_015jWg5oTa6VjANcrtHWqgbu","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/solution.md","content":"# Kubernetes Scheduler Architecture Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n\n### Core Scheduler Files\n- **pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go** — Scheduler struct, main orchestrator managing Cache, SchedulingQueue, Profiles, and NextPod function. Initializes the plugin registry, creates scheduling queue and cache.\n- **pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go** — ScheduleOne() entry point for the main scheduling loop. Contains schedulingCycle() and bindingCycle() implementations. Core scheduling algorithm with filtering, scoring, and binding phases.\n- **pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go** — Event handlers for Pod/Node watchers. Routes events to SchedulingQueue and triggers pod requeuing.\n\n### Framework and Plugin Architecture\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go** — Defines all plugin interfaces (PreEnqueuePlugin, PreFilterPlugin, FilterPlugin, PostFilterPlugin, PreScorePlugin, ScorePlugin, ReservePlugin, PermitPlugin, PreBindPlugin, BindPlugin, PostBindPlugin). Defines Framework interface with plugin execution methods.\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/cycle_state.go** — CycleState struct using sync.Map for thread-safe plugin state storage during a scheduling cycle. Allows plugins to read/write arbitrary data.\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go** — frameworkImpl implementing the Framework interface. Manages plugin initialization, registration at extension points, and orchestration of plugin execution.\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/registry.go** — Plugin registry mapping plugin names to factory functions.\n\n### Scheduling Queue\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go** — SchedulingQueue interface and PriorityQueue implementation. Contains three sub-queues: activeQ (pods being scheduled), podBackoffQ (failed pods with backoff), unschedulablePods (pods rejected by plugins).\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/events.go** — ClusterEvent and queueing hint definitions for efficient pod requeuing based on cluster events.\n\n### Scheduler Cache\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/cache.go** — Cache implementation tracking NodeInfo in a doubly-linked list, assumed pods, and image states. UpdateSnapshot() called at start of each scheduling cycle.\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/snapshot.go** — Snapshot of NodeInfo objects taken at scheduling cycle start. Contains nodeInfoList, nodeInfoMap, and specialized lists for affinity constraints.\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/interface.go** — Cache interface defining contract for scheduler cache operations.\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/node_tree.go** — nodeTree data structure for efficiently finding nodes in the snapshot.\n\n### Plugin Implementations\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/registry.go** — In-tree plugin registry with default plugins (NodeName, NodeUnschedulable, DefaultBinder, etc.).\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/queuesort/** — PrioritySort plugin implementing QueueSortPlugin.\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/noderesources/** — NodeResourcesFit implementing PreFilterPlugin and FilterPlugin.\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/tainttoleration/** — TaintToleration plugin (Filter and PreScore).\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/interpodaffinity/** — InterPodAffinity plugin (PreFilter, Filter, PreScore, Score).\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/defaultbinder/** — DefaultBinder implementing BindPlugin.\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/defaultpreemption/** — DefaultPreemption implementing PostFilterPlugin for preemption logic.\n\n### Supporting Utilities\n- **pkg/scheduler/extender.go** — Out-of-tree scheduler extender support (legacy HTTP-based extensibility).\n- **pkg/scheduler/profile/profile.go** — Profile management creating separate Framework instances per scheduler profile.\n- **pkg/scheduler/metrics/** — Metrics collection for scheduler events and performance.\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### 1. Scheduler Initialization\n```\nNew() in scheduler.go\n  ├─ Creates plugin registry from in-tree and out-of-tree plugins\n  ├─ Builds profiles via profile.NewMap()\n  │  └─ NewFramework() in runtime/framework.go for each profile\n  │     └─ Initializes plugins from registry at extension points\n  ├─ Creates SchedulingQueue via internalqueue.NewSchedulingQueue()\n  ├─ Creates Cache via internalcache.New()\n  ├─ Sets up event handlers via addAllEventHandlers()\n  │  └─ Watches Pod, Node, PVC, Service events\n  └─ Returns fully initialized Scheduler\n```\n\n### 2. Main Scheduling Loop\n```\nScheduler.Run()\n  ├─ Starts SchedulingQueue.Run()\n  ├─ Spawns goroutine calling ScheduleOne() loop\n  │  └─ wait.UntilWithContext(ctx, sched.ScheduleOne, 0)\n  └─ Waits for context cancellation\n\nScheduler.ScheduleOne()\n  ├─ Calls NextPod() → SchedulingQueue.Pop()\n  ├─ Calls frameworkForPod() to get Framework for pod's scheduler name\n  ├─ Creates CycleState\n  ├─ Calls schedulingCycle()\n  │  └─ Returns ScheduleResult or error\n  └─ On success, spawns goroutine for bindingCycle()\n```\n\n### 3. Scheduling Cycle (Synchronous, Main Thread)\n```\nschedulingCycle()\n  ├─ Calls SchedulePod()\n  │  ├─ Cache.UpdateSnapshot() — takes fresh snapshot of node state\n  │  ├─ Calls findNodesThatFitPod()\n  │  │  ├─ Runs PreFilter plugins\n  │  │  ├─ Filters nodes by PreFilterResult\n  │  │  ├─ Evaluates nominated node if present\n  │  │  ├─ Calls findNodesThatPassFilters()\n  │  │  │  └─ Runs Filter plugins on all nodes in parallel\n  │  │  └─ Runs extender filters\n  │  ├─ Runs PreScore plugins\n  │  ├─ Runs Score plugins on feasible nodes\n  │  ├─ Selects best-scored node\n  │  └─ Returns ScheduleResult with suggested host\n  ├─ On failure, runs PostFilter plugins (preemption)\n  ├─ Calls assume() — adds pod to Cache with node binding\n  ├─ Runs Reserve plugins\n  ├─ Runs Permit plugins (may return Wait status)\n  └─ Returns ScheduleResult and assumed pod\n```\n\n### 4. Binding Cycle (Asynchronous, Separate Goroutine)\n```\nbindingCycle()\n  ├─ Calls WaitOnPermit() — waits if Permit plugins returned Wait\n  ├─ Runs PreBind plugins\n  ├─ Calls bind() — executes Bind plugins\n  │  └─ Default: DefaultBinder creates PodBinding\n  ├─ On Bind success:\n  │  ├─ Runs PostBind plugins\n  │  └─ Returns success\n  └─ On error:\n     ├─ Calls handleBindingCycleError()\n     ├─ Runs Unreserve plugins\n     ├─ Cache.ForgetPod() — removes pod assumption\n     └─ Requeues pod via MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()\n```\n\n### 5. Event-Driven Requeuing\n```\nEvent Handlers (Pod/Node watchers)\n  ├─ Pod events → triggers pod requeue\n  ├─ Node events → triggers queueing hints\n  │  └─ Plugins implement EnqueueExtensions\n  │     └─ Advises which pods to requeue based on event type\n  └─ Events queued in SchedulingQueue.inFlightEvents\n     └─ Processed after in-flight pod's scheduling completes\n```\n\n## Architecture Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns\n\n1. **Two-Phase Scheduling Design**\n   - **Scheduling Cycle**: Synchronous, deterministic, locks Cache\n   - **Binding Cycle**: Asynchronous, non-blocking, allows next scheduling cycle to start\n   - **Assumption Step**: Pod assumed in Cache before binding, enabling pipeline parallelism\n\n2. **Plugin Framework Pattern**\n   - **Extension Points**: 12 well-defined points where plugins inject behavior\n   - **Registry Pattern**: Plugins registered at startup, loaded from configuration\n   - **Chain of Responsibility**: Plugins executed in order at each extension point\n   - **Fail-Fast**: First plugin failure aborts cycle (except informational plugins)\n\n3. **State Management**\n   - **CycleState**: Thread-safe map (sync.Map) for per-cycle plugin state\n   - **Cache**: In-memory representation of cluster state (nodes, pods, volumes)\n   - **Snapshot**: Immutable view of Cache taken at cycle start, used throughout cycle\n\n4. **Priority Queue Strategy**\n   - **Active Queue**: Pods ready for scheduling\n   - **Backoff Queue**: Pods waiting for backoff period to expire\n   - **Unschedulable Queue**: Pods with unresolvable issues (5-min timeout)\n   - **Queueing Hints**: Smart requeuing based on cluster events (feature gated)\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n**Scheduler**\n- Orchestrates the scheduling pipeline\n- Manages NextPod function and retry loops\n- Handles failure scenarios and error callbacks\n- Maintains percentage-of-nodes optimization\n\n**Framework (frameworkImpl)**\n- Initializes and manages plugins\n- Calls plugins at each extension point in correct order\n- Manages waiting pods and permit plugin logic\n- Provides Handle interface for plugin access to cluster state\n\n**SchedulingQueue (PriorityQueue)**\n- Manages pod lifecycle (pending → active → scheduled → done)\n- Implements priority ordering via QueueSort plugins\n- Tracks in-flight pods and received events\n- Requeues pods based on cluster events and queueing hints\n\n**Cache (cacheImpl)**\n- Maintains in-memory cluster state (nodes, pods, volumes, images)\n- Manages assumed pods with TTL-based expiration\n- Maintains doubly-linked list for generation tracking\n- Provides efficient snapshot for read operations\n\n**CycleState**\n- Provides thread-safe plugin state storage (sync.Map)\n- Allows plugins to read/write arbitrary data per cycle\n- Tracks skip sets for Filter and Score plugins\n- Records plugin metrics sampling decisions\n\n### Data Flow Through Scheduling\n\n```\n┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│                        SCHEDULING CYCLE                          │\n└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n\n1. SchedulingQueue.Pop() → QueuedPodInfo\n2. Create CycleState (per-cycle plugin state)\n3. Cache.UpdateSnapshot() → NodeSnapshot\n4. RunPreFilterPlugins(state, pod) → PreFilterResult\n   - May filter out nodes\n5. RunFilterPlugins(state, pod, nodeInfo) × N nodes (parallel)\n   - Returns feasible nodes\n6. RunPreScorePlugins(state, pod, feasibleNodes)\n7. RunScorePlugins(state, pod, nodeName) × feasibleNodes (parallel)\n   - Normalizes scores per plugin\n8. SelectHost(scores) → Selected node\n9. Cache.AssumedPod(pod, node) → Updates cache\n10. RunReservePlugins(state, pod, node)\n11. RunPermitPlugins(state, pod, node) → may return Wait\n\n┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│                        BINDING CYCLE                             │\n│              (Runs asynchronously in separate goroutine)         │\n└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n\n1. WaitOnPermit(pod) — blocks if Permit returned Wait\n2. RunPreBindPlugins(state, pod, node)\n3. RunBindPlugins(state, pod, node) → creates Binding object\n4. API Server accepts binding → pod scheduled\n5. RunPostBindPlugins(state, pod, node)\n6. SchedulingQueue.Done(pod.UID)\n```\n\n### Plugin Framework Extension Points\n\n**Pre-Scheduling**\n- **PreEnqueue**: Lightweight filter before adding pod to activeQ\n- **QueueSort**: Determines pod ordering in activeQ (exactly one required)\n\n**Scheduling Cycle**\n- **PreFilter**: Early validation, may return filtered node set\n- **Filter**: Predicate evaluation (node compatibility)\n- **PostFilter**: Preemption logic when pod doesn't fit\n- **PreScore**: Informational extension point before scoring\n- **Score**: Rank nodes (normalized to 0-100)\n- **Reserve**: Reserve resources in plugin state (must support Unreserve)\n- **Permit**: Final approval before binding (may return Wait for external approval)\n\n**Binding Cycle**\n- **PreBind**: Final pre-binding checks\n- **Bind**: Persist binding (default creates PodBinding)\n- **PostBind**: Informational extension point after binding\n\n### Interface Contracts\n\n**Framework.Handle Interface** (passed to plugins)\n```go\n// Plugins can access:\n- SnapshotSharedLister() — read-only cluster state snapshot\n- ClientSet() — Kubernetes API client\n- SharedInformerFactory() — event-driven cluster state\n- Extenders() — out-of-tree extender plugins\n- EventRecorder() — emit events to API server\n- IterateOverWaitingPods() — waiting permits\n```\n\n**Plugin State via CycleState**\n```go\n// Pre-Filter plugins write state, Filter plugins read and may modify\nstate.Write(key, pluginSpecificData)  // write once\nstate.Read(key)                        // read many times\nstate.Delete(key)                      // cleanup\n```\n\n### Interaction Between Key Components\n\n**SchedulingQueue ↔ Cache**\n- Queue pops pods for scheduling\n- Scheduling cycle assumes pod in cache\n- On failure, ForgetPod removes assumption\n- Events from cache handlers trigger queue requeuing\n\n**Cache ↔ Framework (via Snapshot)**\n- Cache creates Snapshot at cycle start\n- Framework provides Snapshot to Handle interface\n- Plugins read nodes, pods, volumes from Snapshot\n- Plugins cannot modify Snapshot (immutable view)\n\n**Framework ↔ CycleState**\n- Framework creates CycleState per scheduling cycle\n- Passes CycleState to all plugins at all extension points\n- PreFilter plugins initialize cycle state\n- Filter/Score plugins read and build on PreFilter state\n\n**Scheduler ↔ FailureHandler**\n- Scheduler invokes FailureHandler on scheduling failure\n- Handler examines failure reason and metrics\n- May implement backoff, requeuing, or preemption logic\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler uses a **plugin-based two-phase architecture** where scheduling (synchronous) and binding (asynchronous) phases are decoupled through the assumption step. The **SchedulingQueue** manages pod flow through three states (active/backoff/unschedulable), while the **Cache** maintains cluster state and enables **snapshot-based consistency** during scheduling cycles. The **Framework** orchestrates **12 extension points** where plugins can inject filtering, scoring, resource reservation, and binding logic. **CycleState** enables plugins to share per-cycle state, and **EnqueueExtensions** provide efficient event-driven requeuing based on cluster changes. This architecture achieves throughput via asynchronous binding and parallelism in filtering/scoring while maintaining scheduling determinism through snapshot isolation.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1141,"cache_read_input_tokens":90697,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1141},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"9a6420d3-4a14-43c0-adb8-a10c7bd0d23a","uuid":"ebc6cf83-b498-4dc4-a14b-b15d529aae60"}

Contains nodeInfoList, nodeInfoMap, and specialized lists for affinity constraints.\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/interface.go** — Cache interface defining contract for scheduler cache operations.\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/node_tree.go** — nodeTree data structure for efficiently finding nodes in the snapshot.\n\n### Plugin Implementations\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/registry.go** — In-tree plugin registry with default plugins (NodeName, NodeUnschedulable, DefaultBinder, etc.).\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/queuesort/** — PrioritySort plugin implementing QueueSortPlugin.\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/noderesources/** — NodeResourcesFit implementing PreFilterPlugin and FilterPlugin.\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/tainttoleration/** — TaintToleration plugin (Filter and PreScore).\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/interpodaffinity/** — InterPodAffinity plugin (PreFilter, Filter, PreScore, Score).\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/defaultbinder/** — DefaultBinder implementing BindPlugin.\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/defaultpreemption/** — DefaultPreemption implementing PostFilterPlugin for preemption logic.\n\n### Supporting Utilities\n- **pkg/scheduler/extender.go** — Out-of-tree scheduler extender support (legacy HTTP-based extensibility).\n- **pkg/scheduler/profile/profile.go** — Profile management creating separate Framework instances per scheduler profile.\n- **pkg/scheduler/metrics/** — Metrics collection for scheduler events and performance.\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### 1. Scheduler Initialization\n```\nNew() in scheduler.go\n  ├─ Creates plugin registry from in-tree and out-of-tree plugins\n  ├─ Builds profiles via profile.NewMap()\n  │  └─ NewFramework() in runtime/framework.go for each profile\n  │     └─ Initializes plugins from registry at extension points\n  ├─ Creates SchedulingQueue via internalqueue.NewSchedulingQueue()\n  ├─ Creates Cache via internalcache.New()\n  ├─ Sets up event handlers via addAllEventHandlers()\n  │  └─ Watches Pod, Node, PVC, Service events\n  └─ Returns fully initialized Scheduler\n```\n\n### 2. Main Scheduling Loop\n```\nScheduler.Run()\n  ├─ Starts SchedulingQueue.Run()\n  ├─ Spawns goroutine calling ScheduleOne() loop\n  │  └─ wait.UntilWithContext(ctx, sched.ScheduleOne, 0)\n  └─ Waits for context cancellation\n\nScheduler.ScheduleOne()\n  ├─ Calls NextPod() → SchedulingQueue.Pop()\n  ├─ Calls frameworkForPod() to get Framework for pod's scheduler name\n  ├─ Creates CycleState\n  ├─ Calls schedulingCycle()\n  │  └─ Returns ScheduleResult or error\n  └─ On success, spawns goroutine for bindingCycle()\n```\n\n### 3. Scheduling Cycle (Synchronous, Main Thread)\n```\nschedulingCycle()\n  ├─ Calls SchedulePod()\n  │  ├─ Cache.UpdateSnapshot() — takes fresh snapshot of node state\n  │  ├─ Calls findNodesThatFitPod()\n  │  │  ├─ Runs PreFilter plugins\n  │  │  ├─ Filters nodes by PreFilterResult\n  │  │  ├─ Evaluates nominated node if present\n  │  │  ├─ Calls findNodesThatPassFilters()\n  │  │  │  └─ Runs Filter plugins on all nodes in parallel\n  │  │  └─ Runs extender filters\n  │  ├─ Runs PreScore plugins\n  │  ├─ Runs Score plugins on feasible nodes\n  │  ├─ Selects best-scored node\n  │  └─ Returns ScheduleResult with suggested host\n  ├─ On failure, runs PostFilter plugins (preemption)\n  ├─ Calls assume() — adds pod to Cache with node binding\n  ├─ Runs Reserve plugins\n  ├─ Runs Permit plugins (may return Wait status)\n  └─ Returns ScheduleResult and assumed pod\n```\n\n### 4. Binding Cycle (Asynchronous, Separate Goroutine)\n```\nbindingCycle()\n  ├─ Calls WaitOnPermit() — waits if Permit plugins returned Wait\n  ├─ Runs PreBind plugins\n  ├─ Calls bind() — executes Bind plugins\n  │  └─ Default: DefaultBinder creates PodBinding\n  ├─ On Bind success:\n  │  ├─ Runs PostBind plugins\n  │  └─ Returns success\n  └─ On error:\n     ├─ Calls handleBindingCycleError()\n     ├─ Runs Unreserve plugins\n     ├─ Cache.ForgetPod() — removes pod assumption\n     └─ Requeues pod via MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()\n```\n\n### 5. Event-Driven Requeuing\n```\nEvent Handlers (Pod/Node watchers)\n  ├─ Pod events → triggers pod requeue\n  ├─ Node events → triggers queueing hints\n  │  └─ Plugins implement EnqueueExtensions\n  │     └─ Advises which pods to requeue based on event type\n  └─ Events queued in SchedulingQueue.inFlightEvents\n     └─ Processed after in-flight pod's scheduling completes\n```\n\n## Architecture Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns\n\n1. **Two-Phase Scheduling Design**\n   - **Scheduling Cycle**: Synchronous, deterministic, locks Cache\n   - **Binding Cycle**: Asynchronous, non-blocking, allows next scheduling cycle to start\n   - **Assumption Step**: Pod assumed in Cache before binding, enabling pipeline parallelism\n\n2. **Plugin Framework Pattern**\n   - **Extension Points**: 12 well-defined points where plugins inject behavior\n   - **Registry Pattern**: Plugins registered at startup, loaded from configuration\n   - **Chain of Responsibility**: Plugins executed in order at each extension point\n   - **Fail-Fast**: First plugin failure aborts cycle (except informational plugins)\n\n3. **State Management**\n   - **CycleState**: Thread-safe map (sync.Map) for per-cycle plugin state\n   - **Cache**: In-memory representation of cluster state (nodes, pods, volumes)\n   - **Snapshot**: Immutable view of Cache taken at cycle start, used throughout cycle\n\n4. **Priority Queue Strategy**\n   - **Active Queue**: Pods ready for scheduling\n   - **Backoff Queue**: Pods waiting for backoff period to expire\n   - **Unschedulable Queue**: Pods with unresolvable issues (5-min timeout)\n   - **Queueing Hints**: Smart requeuing based on cluster events (feature gated)\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n**Scheduler**\n- Orchestrates the scheduling pipeline\n- Manages NextPod function and retry loops\n- Handles failure scenarios and error callbacks\n- Maintains percentage-of-nodes optimization\n\n**Framework (frameworkImpl)**\n- Initializes and manages plugins\n- Calls plugins at each extension point in correct order\n- Manages waiting pods and permit plugin logic\n- Provides Handle interface for plugin access to cluster state\n\n**SchedulingQueue (PriorityQueue)**\n- Manages pod lifecycle (pending → active → scheduled → done)\n- Implements priority ordering via QueueSort plugins\n- Tracks in-flight pods and received events\n- Requeues pods based on cluster events and queueing hints\n\n**Cache (cacheImpl)**\n- Maintains in-memory cluster state (nodes, pods, volumes, images)\n- Manages assumed pods with TTL-based expiration\n- Maintains doubly-linked list for generation tracking\n- Provides efficient snapshot for read operations\n\n**CycleState**\n- Provides thread-safe plugin state storage (sync.Map)\n- Allows plugins to read/write arbitrary data per cycle\n- Tracks skip sets for Filter and Score plugins\n- Records plugin metrics sampling decisions\n\n### Data Flow Through Scheduling\n\n```\n┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│                        SCHEDULING CYCLE                          │\n└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n\n1. SchedulingQueue.Pop() → QueuedPodInfo\n2. Create CycleState (per-cycle plugin state)\n3. Cache.UpdateSnapshot() → NodeSnapshot\n4. RunPreFilterPlugins(state, pod) → PreFilterResult\n   - May filter out nodes\n5. RunFilterPlugins(state, pod, nodeInfo) × N nodes (parallel)\n   - Returns feasible nodes\n6. RunPreScorePlugins(state, pod, feasibleNodes)\n7. RunScorePlugins(state, pod, nodeName) × feasibleNodes (parallel)\n   - Normalizes scores per plugin\n8. SelectHost(scores) → Selected node\n9. Cache.AssumedPod(pod, node) → Updates cache\n10. RunReservePlugins(state, pod, node)\n11. RunPermitPlugins(state, pod, node) → may return Wait\n\n┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│                        BINDING CYCLE                             │\n│              (Runs asynchronously in separate goroutine)         │\n└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n\n1. WaitOnPermit(pod) — blocks if Permit returned Wait\n2. RunPreBindPlugins(state, pod, node)\n3. RunBindPlugins(state, pod, node) → creates Binding object\n4. API Server accepts binding → pod scheduled\n5. RunPostBindPlugins(state, pod, node)\n6. SchedulingQueue.Done(pod.UID)\n```\n\n### Plugin Framework Extension Points\n\n**Pre-Scheduling**\n- **PreEnqueue**: Lightweight filter before adding pod to activeQ\n- **QueueSort**: Determines pod ordering in activeQ (exactly one required)\n\n**Scheduling Cycle**\n- **PreFilter**: Early validation, may return filtered node set\n- **Filter**: Predicate evaluation (node compatibility)\n- **PostFilter**: Preemption logic when pod doesn't fit\n- **PreScore**: Informational extension point before scoring\n- **Score**: Rank nodes (normalized to 0-100)\n- **Reserve**: Reserve resources in plugin state (must support Unreserve)\n- **Permit**: Final approval before binding (may return Wait for external approval)\n\n**Binding Cycle**\n- **PreBind**: Final pre-binding checks\n- **Bind**: Persist binding (default creates PodBinding)\n- **PostBind**: Informational extension point after binding\n\n### Interface Contracts\n\n**Framework.Handle Interface** (passed to plugins)\n```go\n// Plugins can access:\n- SnapshotSharedLister() — read-only cluster state snapshot\n- ClientSet() — Kubernetes API client\n- SharedInformerFactory() — event-driven cluster state\n- Extenders() — out-of-tree extender plugins\n- EventRecorder() — emit events to API server\n- IterateOverWaitingPods() — waiting permits\n```\n\n**Plugin State via CycleState**\n```go\n// Pre-Filter plugins write state, Filter plugins read and may modify\nstate.Write(key, pluginSpecificData)  // write once\nstate.Read(key)                        // read many times\nstate.Delete(key)                      // cleanup\n```\n\n### Interaction Between Key Components\n\n**SchedulingQueue ↔ Cache**\n- Queue pops pods for scheduling\n- Scheduling cycle assumes pod in cache\n- On failure, ForgetPod removes assumption\n- Events from cache handlers trigger queue requeuing\n\n**Cache ↔ Framework (via Snapshot)**\n- Cache creates Snapshot at cycle start\n- Framework provides Snapshot to Handle interface\n- Plugins read nodes, pods, volumes from Snapshot\n- Plugins cannot modify Snapshot (immutable view)\n\n**Framework ↔ CycleState**\n- Framework creates CycleState per scheduling cycle\n- Passes CycleState to all plugins at all extension points\n- PreFilter plugins initialize cycle state\n- Filter/Score plugins read and build on PreFilter state\n\n**Scheduler ↔ FailureHandler**\n- Scheduler invokes FailureHandler on scheduling failure\n- Handler examines failure reason and metrics\n- May implement backoff, requeuing, or preemption logic\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler uses a **plugin-based two-phase architecture** where scheduling (synchronous) and binding (asynchronous) phases are decoupled through the assumption step. The **SchedulingQueue** manages pod flow through three states (active/backoff/unschedulable), while the **Cache** maintains cluster state and enables **snapshot-based consistency** during scheduling cycles. The **Framework** orchestrates **12 extension points** where plugins can inject filtering, scoring, resource reservation, and binding logic. **CycleState** enables plugins to share per-cycle state, and **EnqueueExtensions** provide efficient event-driven requeuing based on cluster changes. This architecture achieves throughput via asynchronous binding and parallelism in filtering/scoring while maintaining scheduling determinism through snapshot isolation.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
